AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH I PROJECT
RESEARCH PROGRAM FOR FARMING SYSTEMS IN AMAZONIA (NORTH)
I. INTRODUCTION
A. Agricultural Importance of the Region
1.        This vast region of 3.58 million kmn  represents 42% of total land
area of Brazil and encompasses one of the world's great hydrographic basins.
It is sparsely populated, approximately 1.02 persons per km,2 and the popu-
lation of 3.6 million represents only 3.9% of Brazil's total population. It
comprises three states: Acre, Amazonas and Para, and three federal territo-
ries; Rondonia, Roraima and Amapa. Agriculture plays a relatively small
role in the economic activity of the area, accounting for only 22.2% of
regional GNP. The region as a whole accounts for 2.1% of Brazil's GNP (1968).
Population Density
2.        As indicated by the following table, population density is extremely
low (1970 figures):
Area                                 Population
State or Territory               (km2)           Population        Density per km2
Acre                       152,589           218,006               1.43
Amapa                      140,276           116,480               0.83
Amazonas                 1,564,445           960,934               0.61
Para                     1,248,042         2,197,072               1.76
Rondonia                   243,004           116,620               0.48
Roraima                    230,104            41,638               0.18
TOTAL         3,578,460         3,650,750               1.02
BRAZIL                   8,511,965        94,508,554              11.10
Source: Anuario Estatistico do Brazil, 1974.



ANNEX 14
Page 2
Physical Aspects
3.        The area has been the subject of several broad surveys, mainly
by aerial and satellite photography, but detailed observations by ground
survey have largely been limited to the populated pockets where water
or road transportation has permitted access.
4.        Climate.  The area can be broadly classified into three distinct
regions: (a) the hot, humid equatorial tropics without a pronounced dry
season in the west and north; (b) the hot, humid equatorial region, with
a short (winter) dry season, mainly in the eastern portion of Roraima
Territory and stretching east in a narrow belt to the Amazon basin, north of
Belem, and (c) the hot, tropical climate to the southeast, stretching as
far south as Cuiaba, Mato Grosso, and having a marked dry season of three
to four months. There is a wide range in temperatures, from minimums of
12 to 160C and highs of 34 to 440C. Annual rainfall varies between
1,500 mm to 3,000 mm and up to 4,000 mm has been recorded in northern
Amapa.
5.        Soils.  Broad soil reconnaissance has been carried out on only
seven percent (557,000 km2) of the entire area, with detailed surveys of
perhaps 25% (121,000 km2) of that region being complete. Contrary to popu-
lar belief, the soil types are by no means homogeneous, and this presents
several problems when agricultural development of the area is being con-
sidered. The major broad classification of the soils to be found in the
region are: yellow and red to deep-red latosols; concretionary laterites,
black and yellow podzols; grumosols; hydromorphic laterites, humid gleys,
alluvials of recent fluvial action by the main rivers; and the saline soils
in the main drainage deltas. From an agricultural viewpoint, the most prom-
ising soils are frequently the yellow latosols, which are well drained and
are heavily forested. On removing the forest, however, the thin cap of
organic soil is quickly oxidized and the soils, in general, are found to
be of low fertility but of good structure and suitable for agriculture when
carefully managed.
Principal Agricultural Regions
6.        Although not clearly defined, and obviously selected more on the
basis of access and limited infrastructure than for selected land use, one
or two agricultural regions can be identified. In general, the regions are
located along the river banks, at easily accessible points, and rely on a
few major urban centers such as Belem, l4anaus, Santarem, Macapa, Porto Velho,
Boa Vista and Rio Branco. These townships provide a base both for necessary
supplies and for markets for the agricultural products. The regions are
further typified by two main types of agricultural enterprise as follows:



ANNEX 14
Page 3
(a) Livestock production. Most livestock operations are located
in the states of Para, Amazonas and Acre. Typically, these
operations use unimproved pasturage, which appears after the
felling of the forest stand. The main enterprise of these
regions is beef cattle or buffalo for meat and milk. Areas of
high ground surrounding the farm building may additionally be
used to cultivate small quantities of subsistence crops, such
as rice, cassava, maize and beans. Where the elevated plains
are sufficiently high above the water table, commercial crops
of sugarcane, black pepper and jute may be grown.
(b) Extractive Agriculture. The term is used to indicate the
harvesting of native, uncultivated species which occur spon-
taneously but frequently in fairly large quantities within
the natural forest stand. Good examples of the products are
rubber, Brazil nuts, and vegetable oils, mainly from palm
species, and hunting operations for the commercial production
of skins from wild animals to be found in the forest.
7.        In addition to livestock and extractive agriculture, the following
10 field crops are important for the population centers in Amazonia: cassava,
black pepper, rice, corn, beans, banana, citrus, sugarcane, jute and tobacco.
With the exception of black pepper and jute, all crops are considered mainly
within the framework of subsistence agriculture, or for marketing in small
quantities within the local market structure. With few exceptions, these
crops are grown with only limited recourse to modern technology. The main
exception is black pepper, where the Japanese have introduced many innovative
procedures.
B. Current Status of Research
8.        The National Research Council (CNPq) has played a leading role in
coordinating biological research in the general area, but its interest has
been narrowly scientific rather than applied and it has tended to guide the
programs of the Institute for Research for Amazonia (INPA), the Regional
Survey Program (RADAM) of the Ministry of Mines and Energy, and the research
program of the Institute for Agricultural Research of the Western Amazon
(IPEAAOC) towards cataloging of natural resources of the area. During
recent years, there has also been an increasing awareness of the need to
preserve the delicate biotic balance of this vast region, which is the largest
area of virgin rainforest in the hemisphere, and one which man has as yet
only partially explored. In recent years, the cataloging of forest reserves
has been undertaken by the Brazilian Institute for Forestry Development (IDBF)Y
None of these studies, however, has attempted to link the resources of the
area to rational land use on the basis of well planned farming systems research.



ANNEX 14
Page 4
On the other hand, the stations linked to the old National Department for
Agricultural Research (DNPEA), namely, the Institute for Agricultural
Research in the North (IPEAN) and the Institute for Agricultural Research
in Western Amazonia (IPEAAOc), have carried out research programs related
to specific crops and the latter (IPEAAOc) has recently begun research
on farming systems and a study of their effect on the virgin forest complex
of the area west of Manaus.
9.        Achievements have, admittedly, been limited in the past, as is
evidenced by the fact that this huge land area, 42% of the national total,
produces only some 2.1% of GNP, with agricultural production amounting to
only about US$27.8 million. 1/ Agriculture is characterized by low levels
of production, low levels of mechanization and of fertilizer consumption
(5.6 kg/ha on cultivated land), a low level of technology and a concentra-
tion of the population in extractive agriculture. Added to this is the
highly unbalanced pattern of land tenure, i.e., 10% of holdings account for
83% of the land area, with 90% of all farms less than 100 ha in size.  Most
of the region's agricultural activity is in the state of Para.
10.       Population distribution, socio-economic factors and lack of
infrastructure in the area obviously present formidable obstacles to be
overcome before even modest advances can be made in improving agricultural
production in the region. In addition, it is now generally accepted that
the agricultural frontiers should hne advanred qlnwlv and nrily aufter ronrzicir-
able thought has been given to ensuring adequate protection of the delicate
environmental balance of the region. Other difficulties relate to methods
of improving yields within the concepts of extractive agriculture and the
need to select cultivated crops which are compatible to the preservation
of the environment.
II. THE RESEARCH PROGRAM FOR FARMING SYSTEMS IN AMAZONIA (NORTH)
A. General Description
11.       Although the project area of influence has been designated as the
entire northern region (Amazonia), it is obvious that development must proceed
gradually from the few population nuclei where minimal infrastructure has
provided a foothold for agricultural production. The program would of necessity
have strong linkages to the national programs for the development of the region.
These are outlined in the second National Development Plan 1975-1979 (PNDII) and
comprise the establishment of 15 development poles. These selected areas lie
principally in southern Para and northern Mato Grosso and Goias states. Initial
1/   Source:  Annual Statistics:  Brasil (IBGE), 1973.



ANNEX 14
Page 5
emphasis would be placed on livestock production and selected crops such as
rubber, sugarcane, cacao, oil palm, rice, black pepper and tropical fruits.
The program designated POLAMAZONIA would be funded through the Program
for National Integration (PIN), the Program for Land Distribution and Agri-
cultural Incentives in the North and Northeast (PROTERRA), and the Fund for
Development of Integrated Projects (FDPI). Implicit within the program is
the policy of national development of the land and mineral and forest resources
of the area.
Program Goals
12.       Broad program goals would be to diversify greatly the opportunities
for developing agricultural enterprises through:
(a) adoption and improvement of existing crops to provide greater
flexibility in the utilization of natural resources through
crop rotation and farming systems technology;
(b) providing linkage to the appropriate commodity centers to
obtain new technology for the increase of yields of the
subsistence crops, such as cassava, beans, rice, maize; and
(c) introduction of high value specialty cash crops, such as
Brazil nut, black pepper, "guarana" 1/ and rubber where
applicable to raise the income level of the farmer.
13.       Since considerable facilities and expertise already exist for
carrying out forestry studies at the IDBF and INPA institutes, concentration
on food, fiber and vegetative oil crops at the Belem and Manaus (IPEAAOc)
centers would avoid duplication of effort in this area. Conversely, INPA and
IDBF would be encouraged to refer all problems concerning crops and animal
husbandry to the Belem Agricultural Research Center for the Amazon, where
the farming systems research program is to be headquartered.
Program Components
14.        Components of the Program for Farming Systems Research for the
Amazonia Region to be provided under the project are as follows:
(a) completion of the necessary laboratory and research
facilities at the headquarters station, Belem;
(b) research farm development at the station;
(c) provision of equipment, furniture and vehicles for use at
the Belem station;
1/   A tree crop, the fruits (seeds) of which are used in the manufacture of
a popular soft drink of the same name.



ANNEX 14
Page 6
(d) library documentation and information services;
(e) technical services, including consultants, fellowship and
short course training programs; and
(f) establishment costs of the program during a five-year period.
Details of the investments proposed are given in Tables 1, 2 and 3.
B. Detailed Features
15.       The research program would be designed to achieve the following
broad objectives:
(a) based on the existing inventories of natural resource potential
already widely available from previous studies, select areas
suitable for crop and livestock production programs, with an
emphasis on resource management as opposed to additional resource
inventories and basic science;
(b) based on regional development programs, select the combinations
of crops and livestock adaptable to each region and micro-region;
(c) after crop priorities have been established, develop farming
systems, incorporating these crops, consistent with the
preservation of the basic soil, water, and plant relationships;
(d) with the assistance of producers, and the respective commodity
program teams for the crops concerned, formulate extension
bulletins for use by farmers at various levels of inputs, i.e.,
land, capital, labor, credit, market facilities, and the like;
(e) based on basic data on forest species being harvested in the
wild state, devise methods by which such sources of income
can be increased without permanent alteration to the natural
forest complex; and
(f) adopt and adapt existing livestock husbandry techniques to
local conditions designed to improve returns from mixed
beef/dairy herds and further develop the use of water buffalo
in the area.



ANNEX 14
Page 7
C. Organization and Management
16.       The Research Program for Farming Systems in Amazonia would be head-
quartered at Belem, Para. The station director would have overall respon-
sibility for administration of the headquarters station and would represent
ENIBRAPA for community relations at the center. He would be assisted by an
advisory council 1/ and two associate directors--one for adm4inistrative
services, usually functioning as the financial and procurement officer, and
one for the implementation of the research program.
17.       The associate director for research, as team leader/coordinator,
would have full responsibility for all technical aspects of the program
and would provide the necessary leadership for program planning, budgeting,
execution and evaluation, coordination with satellite stations (UEPAEs) and
other cooperating institutions concerned with research on farming systems
and the application of new technology to production techniques. This would
be achieved through contacts between the team leader and representatives
of the appropriate research programs at these stations. An annual workshop
would be held at which current activities would be evaluated and plans for
the research program for the coming years would be made. Inputs from
producers would be obtained at such workshops or field days in the distinct
sub-areas of major production. As a member of the advisory council, the
associate director for research would provide the necessary liaison between
the council and producers (see also Annex 3).
Project MIonitoring and Evaluation
18.       Based on the crops which are selected to form part of the farming
systems research in the area, the program leader/coordinator would form a
coordinating committee with representatives from the commodity centers
concerned and the farming systems specialists from the satellite stations
(UEPAEs) in the area. This coordinating team would assist the program leader
in the formulation of the research program and would also contribute sugges-
tions from producers of the specific crops being studied. This same committee
would select a few of its members to participate in the annual internal evalua-
tion review of the research program. In addition, there would be periodic
(two to three years) external review in which international consultants would be
asked to participate. The same coordinating teams, with representatives
from farmers and collaborating research institutions, would formulate the
technological packages of basic farming systems information for delivery to
the UEPAEs and state level extension agencies.
1/   The advisory council would normally comprise seven to nine members but
composition might vary according to location (see Annex 17 for example
of membership).



ANNEX 14
Page 8
Research Facilities
19.       The headquarters for farming systems research for Amazonia located
at Belem would have 6,500 ha of land. This station already has sufficient
administrative and laboratory facilities so no civil works would be involved
under the project. Additional equipment would be supplied as indicated under
project components. The main satellite stations would be situated at Manaus
(with 3,000 ha) and at Altamira (with 500 ha) where the adaptation of technol-
ogy to micro-regional differences and on-farm demonstrations would take
place (see Table 4).
Collaborating Institutions
20.       It is expected that the results of basic biological, geological
and hydrologic research currently being carried out at INPA (Manaus) would
be available to the Belem station on a cooperative basis. The Brazilian
Institute for Forestry Development would collaborate on forestry aspects of
the program in a similar way.
University Contract Research
21.       Performance of university contract research would depend upon the
specific needs of the research program as a whole. If required, it would be
carried out on the basis of requests from EMBRAPA to the university most
capable of handling the work. Projects designated for university contract
research would be clearly defined, be of rather short duration, and concern
basic research to provide necessary linkage to ongoing long-term research
within the farming systems program. The Federal University of Para in Belem,
is well located to carry out such projects, but it is unclear whether its areas
of study would coincide with the broad concepts of farming systems research.
Data on economic factors of production, however, could well pravide basic
study projects in which new crops are to be introduced.
D. Staffing
22.       Staffing requirements for the farming systems program of research at
the Belem Station would be 81 professionals and 40 administrative support
personnel. It is expected that, as necessary, research teams wzould carry out
work at the commodity research centers and UEPAEs within the area of project
influence (Amazonia) to test and demonstrate new farming systems techniques
developed at the center. It is estimated that 20% of staff requirements are
already available at Belem; however, a comprehensive in-service training
program would be necessary to train staff in farming systems technology as
quickly as possible (see also Table 5).



ANNEX 14
Page 9
E. Training and Fellowship Program
23.       A training officer would be available at the Belem station to
assist in the selection of candidates for the fellowship program. The project
would provide funds for the training of 30 staff members for the M.Sc. degree
and eight to the Ph.D. level. In addition, provision would be made for short
training courses for 15 selected staff members in specific areas of study
related to the program (Table 2).
F. Consultants
24.       Since the concept of applied farming systems research, particularly
in the planning stage, is new to the project area a full time research center
consultant would be stationed at Belem for three years. The consultant chosen
should have had experience with similar research projects at a Tropical Re-
search Institute, such as the International Institute for Tropical Agriculture
(IITA) Ibadan, Nigeria. In addition, 2.0 man-years of short-term consultancy
services would be provided (Table 2).
G. Linkages to International Centers
25.       In matters relating to farming systems technology for the humid
tropics, an interchange of views and of personnel on short-term assignments
would be extremely beneficial to the program. The similar interests of IITA,
Nigeria would indicate that valuable assistance might be obtained from the
outreach program of that center. On a commodity basis, i.e., rice, cassava
and beans, the International Center of Tropical Agriculture (CIAT) at Cali,
Colombia is also well suited to enter into cooperative programs with the
center at Belem. Additionally, the International Livestock Center for Africa
(ILCA), Addis Ababa, Ethiopia is engaged in production (farming systems)
research for the humid and semi-humid tropics, particularly in the field of
range management, and may be in a position to collaborate with the Brazilian
livestock research program for Amazonia.
III. PROGRAM COST ESTIMATES
26.       The cost for the Research Program for Farming Systems in Amazonia
for the five-year period would be approximately US$10.4 million. The
estimated costs are summarized in Tables 1, 2 and 3.
December 15, 1975

AGRICULTURE RESEARCH I PROJECT
Civil Works Program
Civil Works Components
1.        There are four building types, namely:
(a) Agricultural Research Centers (ARC);
(b) National Commodity Centers (NCC);
(c) Unidades de Execucao de Pesquisa de Ambito Estadual
(UEPAE), Type 1, covering three crops; and
(d) UEPAE, Type 2, including animal facilities.
A schedule of accommodation for each center (Appendix 1) has been derived
from the functional programs and the proposed staffing lists (Annexes 3 to
14). These schedules may be refined during the course of overall pL:ojecL
development, but there will be little change in magnitude. The centers will
be planned to permit easy growth and modification to accommodate changes of
function and program over time. At each center, provision has been made for
technology diffusion, together with facilities for preparation of demonstra-
tion materials. In line with a policy decision by EMBRAPA, housing would not
be provided.
Civil Works Implementation
2.        Currently, EMBRAPA does not have personnel, nor established proce-
dures, for implementing civil works projects. The Directorate of Construction
and Installation of the Ministry of Agriculture, which specifically serves
only the departments of that Ministry, will not participate in the proposed
Bank project so it is essential that EMBRAPA establish a Technical Support
Unit (TSU) to administer, not only the Bank-financed project, but also others
with civil works components. The unit should consist of architects and
engineers with supporting staff. In view of the importance of specifying
laboratory equipment and preparing the pre-ordering schedule, officers
having this specific responsibility should be included on the staff. Terms
of Reference for this unit are included as Appendix 2.



ANNEX 15
Page 2
Development Plan Study and Report
3.        In order to provide more precise definition of the civil works com-
ponent in terms of both content and anticipated progress, a Development Plan
should be prepared for each center by EMBRAPA. This should be assembled
in consultation with the Program Advisor, the TSU, and the executive architects
and should cover the following topics, inter alia:
(a)  site development plan for both land and physical facilities;
(b)  soil, subsoil and climatic data, together with topographical
survey;
(c)  more precise definition of the functional program indicating
outline of proposed activities and staff needs;
(d)  schedule of accommodation, refining the material in Appendix 2,
as necessary;
(e)  preliminary list of major laboratory equipment;
(f)  preliminary budget covering land preparation, civil works,
furnishings and equipment; and
(g)  anticipated progress schedule for implementing the construction
program.
(h)  each plan and progress reort would be sent to the Bank for review
and approval.
Professional Services
4.        The technical problems presented by the civil works components are
within the expertise of national architects. No expatriate consultants
would be recommended, provided that the Bank retains the right of approval
of appointments.
Construction Supervision
5.        The executive architects would provide customary periodic supervi-
sion, and, in line with traditional practice, local firms of architects or
engineers would be retained for day-to-day supervision.
Retroactive Financing
6.        To reduce the impact of increasing construction costs, an early start
must be made on architectural work and, hence, construction. To this end,
retroactive financing up to the sum of US$500,000 is recommended to cover the
initial costs of professional fees, which may be incurred before loan approval.
Included are architectural and engineering fees, topographic and soil surveys.



ANNEX 15
Page 3
Sites
7.        Currently, EMBRAPA does not have legal title to all sites at which
construction is proposed. In fact, at several locations, the actual site has
not yet been identified. EMBRAPA would therefore make legal arrangements to
purchase or use the land.
Procurement
8.        Due to the dispersed nature of the components of the civil works
project, transportation difficulties, and the relatively small size of the
construction contracts, it is doubtful that foreign contractors or even major
national contractors would be interested. However, Government procurement
procedures would be followed, contracts would be advertised in the local and
national press and foreign bidders would not be excluded. Work by force
account would be permitted in remote areas where it is difficult to obtain
contractors by competitive bidding. For the procurement of laboratory equip-
ment and other specialized items, standard Government procedures would be
followed and awards would be made taking into consideration local maintenance
potential, including service contracts, in addition to bid price.
Basis of Cost Estimates
9.        Cost estimates as shown in Table 1 have been prepared on the follow-
ing basis:
(a) Using the schedules of accommodation for each center, construction
cost estimates have been prepared by a local architect based on
elemental cost estimates of analogous building types. Estimates
for individual centers have been adjusted for local prices by using
established provincial cost variation factors. It has been assumed
that municipal water and electrical supply will be available at all
centers. The cost of road works, drainage, boundary fencing and
irrigation is carried under the allowance to farm development.
(b) Design and construction contingencies have been included.
(c) At some sites, there are buildings that would be used in connection
with the proposed project. These have been taken into account,
but the minor costs of undertaking these repairs and upgrading
have not been quantified. EMBRAPA would undertake the required
work concurrently with new construction.
(d) In the absence of reliable estimates for laboratory equipment,
gross assumptions have been made.
(e) Furniture costs have been based on unit costs supplied by EMBRAPA
in the light of recent experience.



ANNEX 15
Page 4
(f) Professional fees amount to 6%. This allowance is based on the
fee scale of the Institute of Architects of Brazil and the
conventional fee charged by structural and mechanical services
engineers.
(g) Brazil has a long history of inflation and high rates of escala-
tion of construction costs so that it is virtually impossible
to forecast the degree of escalation during the life of the
proposed project. However, the effective reevaluation of the
US dollar against the cruzeiro has a mitigating effect on the
impact of escalation. In 1975, it was found that the conventional
allowance recommended by Central Projects, plus the effective
reevaluation of the US dollar, equalled the observed escalation
factor. On this basis and on the grounds that the loan would be
made in US dollars, the conventional allowance would be adopted,
namely, 1976, 14%; 1977, 12%; 1978, 12%.

BRAZIL
AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH I PROJECT
RESPONSIBILITIES OF THE TECHNICAL SUPPORT UNIT
The Technical Support Unit (TSU) would be established within
EMBRAPA to handle overall project coordination and liaison with the Bank,
in respect to civil works and equipment. Staffing of the "SU is discussed
in para 2, Annex 15.
In particular, the responsibilities of the TSU would be to:
(a) assist EMBRAPA in assembling the architectural brief for the
executive architects;
(b) assist EMBRAPA with the selection and appointment of the
executive architects and in retaining other professional services;
(c) participate with EMBRAPA and the executive architects in preparing
the Development Plan Report for each of the Research Centers;
(d) in cooperation with the executive architects and engineers,
establish and manage a work program utilizing appropriate program-
ming tools such as network analysis for all activities during the
design, construction, and commissioning phase of the project;
(e) arrange for the review and approval by EMBRAPA and the Bank of,
inter alia, architectural and engineering reports, plans, speci-
fications and equipment lists at the following stages:
(i) schematic design;
(ii) final design; and
(iii) working drawings and contract documents.
(f) participate in the following:
(i) weekly meetings between EMBRAPA and the executive architects
during the design phase;
(ii) monthly progress meetings with the contractors and architects
during the construction phase;



ANNEX 15
Appendix 2
Page 2
(iii) selection and prequalification of contractors;
(iv) approval and supervision of bidding procedures; and
(v) adjudication and award of contracts.
(g) prepare the schedule and budget for laboratory equipment at
each center, establish procurement procedures, ascertain antici-
pated lead time for preparing the pre-ordering schedule;
(h) ensure that furniture is selected and installed according to
specification, as well as ensuring timely procurement in order
that the centers may be commissioned on schedule;
(i) oversee project progress, making weekly reports to EMBRAPA and
quarterly reports to the Bank;
(j) process contractors' bills for payment by EMBRAPA and subsequent
forwarding to the Bank for disbursement; and
(k) prepare a commissioning program, and, at the completion of
construction, participate with the executive architects in
advising EMBRAPA on the acceptance of the completed buildings.
January 29, 1976

BRAZIL
AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH I PROJECT
Project Costs and Disbursements
1.        In order to provide basic information necessary for monitoring
and evaluation of the research programs (Annex 17), costs have been distri-
buted according to commodity and farming systems research programs (Table 1).
A proposed calendar of procurement and disbursement, for calendar years
1976-1980, is given in Tables 2 and 3. The phasing for establishment cost
items is shown in Table 4. Since budgets for the state experiment stations
(UEPAEs) will be a function of the contribution to research programs allocated
by each station, the project costs attributable to each have been calculated
for the 14 stations under the project. These cost distributions, for each
type of UEPAE, are shown in Tables 5 to 10.
Capital Inputs
2.        Year 1 (FY1977) expenditures are expected to include land purchase,
development studies and costs of the technical support unit. Design and
preparation of building plans would be concluded in late FY1977 and construc-
tion would commence, for the UEPAEs, in the third quarter of FY1977 and
continue until the fourth quarter of FY1978. Purchase of equipment, commis-
sioning of facilities, research and field laboratories, library and informa-
tion services would take place in the second quarter of FY1978 for UEPAEs and
the fourth quarter of FY1978 for ARCs and NCCs (see Civil Works Schedule,
Annex 15, Chart 1). Based on the above, the disbursement schedule for these
components was calculated as follows: FY1976 - 1%; FY1977 - 20%; FY1978 - 55%,
and FY1979 - 24%.
Technical Services
3.        Consultants.  It was assumed that 14.5 man-years of consultancy ser-
vices would be required in the first year of operation, 24 man-years during
project years 2 through 4; and 14 man-years during the last year of project
execution.
4.        Fellowships.  The appropriate phasing for this component is pro-
vided in Annex 17, Table 6. The training program for Ph.D. and +M.Sc. fellow-
ships will be phased as follows: year 1 - 25%; year 2 - 30%; year 3 - 25%;
year 4 - 12%; and year 5 - 8%. Since it is expected that short-courses for
in-service training would be later in starting, they have been distributed
accordingly throughout the implementation period.
Establishment Costs
5.        Incremental salaries would be phased in over the five-year project
execution period as follows:  calendar year 1976 - US$3 million; 1977 - US$4.6



ANNEX 16
Page  2
million; 1978 - US$7.2 million; 1979 - US$8.2 million; and 1980 - US$10.1
million. Other incremental operating expenses would show a similar pattern
as they are directly related to the estimated staff development plan. It
is calculated that other operating expenses would amount to 30% of salaries
in the first two years and to 40% of salaries in the following three years
(Table 4).
December 15, 1975

BRAZIL
AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH I PROJECT
ORGANIZATION AND MANAGEMENT
A. Background
StaLu,ury base and Objectives
1.        The Brazilian Agricultural Research Corporation (EHBRAPA) was
created on December 7, 1972, by Law No. 5.85, as a public institution linked
to the Ministry of Agriculture, but also as a legal entity with administra-
tive and financial autonomy. EMBRAPA began operations on April 26, 1973.
2.        EMBRAPA has taken over the functions of the previous National
Department of Agricultural Research (DNPEA) and is responsible for the
coordination and promotion of agricultural research throughout Brazil. It
will establish coordinated, multi-disciplinary national research programs
involving the EMBRAPA research centers, cooperating universities, and state
and private organizations. The nationwide cooperative system is still in the
formative stage, but it is designed to concentrate etforts ot the cooperating
institutions on problems of national, regional and state or local concern.
Priority emphasis will be placed on development of new technologies to make
the nation's agriculture more efficient and productive.
EMBRAPA Finances
3.        EMBRAPA's total assets, mainly properties and facilities transfer-
red to it after its creation in late 1972, amounted to about Cr$1.4 billion
(or roughly US$185 million) as of December 31, 1974. Although it has the
legal status of a public company rather than government department, EfBRAPA
is almost totally dependent upon government budget allocations or government
secured borrowing to finance its operations. EMBRAPA's annual and tri-annual
budgets are subject to government approval as part of the Ministry of Agricul-
ture budgets. In 1974, EMBRAPA's total expenditures were Cr$181.9 million (in
1975 prices, or roughly US$21 million), of which about 4% represented invest-
ments in new facilities, 53% personnel costs, and the remaining 43% materials,
rents, utilities and other miscellaneous expenses, sub-contracts and transfers
(see Table 1). Roughly 72% of EMBRAPA's funding in 1974 came directly
from the Federal Treasury (including allocations from the Ministry of Agricul-
ture's general budget -- partly representing domestic loans -- PROTERRA,
1/ PIN 2/ and other federal funds); approximately another 18% represented
1/   Programa de Redistribuicao de Terras e de Estimulo a Agro-Industria de
Norte e do Nordeste (Program for the Redistribution of Land and Stimula-
tion of Agro-Business in the North and Northeast).
2/   Programa da Integracao Nacional (National Integration Program).



ANNEX 17
Page  2
transfers from special contracts between EMBRAPA and other Brazilian entities
(e.g., SUDENE, BNB, other agencies linked with the Ministry of Agriculture);
about 4% from a USAID loan (see paragraph 6 below); and the remainder from
miscellaneous sources and sales of services and agricultural produce.
4.        EMBRAPA's approved 1975 budget amounted to Cr$495.5 million (or
roughly US$58 million), about triple the 1974 budget. The programmed expendi-
tures of EMBRAPA in 1975 represented about 12.5% of the total programmed
expenditures of the Ministry of Agriculture and its related agencies. The 1975
EMBRAPA program included a very substantial increase in EMBRAPA investments,
reflecting partly the fact that EMBRAPA's previous two years of activities
were focused mainly on consolidating and reorganizing Brazilian agricultural
research rather than on intensifying or expanding it.
Projections for 1976-78 Program
5.        The preliminary budget requests made by EMBRAPA to the Ministry
of Agriculture for the 1976-78 period assume a continued rapid growth in
the total EMBRAPA program. Total expenditures would be about US$82 million
in 1976 and US$98 million in 1977 and would reach US$137 million in 1978.
The composition of expenditures will shift with the expansion of Brazil's
research efforts and, by 1978, the share of fixed investments in total EMBRAPA
expenditures would reach almost 32%. While the regional distribution of the
EMBRAPA program is not yet defined (since, indeed, the projects for some
commodities and regions are still under preparation), preliminary estimates
indicate that roughly half of its program over the medium term will be directed
specifically to the Northeast, North and Central-West regions (with almost
half of that in the Northeast).
6.        Over the next several years, the government hopes to finance a
larger share of the EMBRAPA program with foreign borrowings or assistance
than it has in the past. In 1972, before EMBRAPA was created, USAID made a
US$11.93 million loan to the Government for agricultural research. The loan
covered technical assistance, equipment and training and is expected to be
fully committed in about a year. UNDP has also funded various projects in the
agriculture sector in Brazil, one of which focuses on livestock-related re-
search in the Northeast. EMBRAPA has responsibility for the project, which
was begun in 1971 and which is now working mainly on pasture research. EMBRAPA
is also receiving various special technical assistance or equipment grants
from several countries, including the United States, France, Japan, Germany,
and England. Most are linked to the provision of several specialists or items
of equipment for individual research stations. It is also negotiating similar
technical assistance and exchange agreements with several other countries as
well. In general, these bilateral agreements can be expected to help provide
EMBRAPA with valuable technical assistance, but they are not likely to meet
a significant portion of EMBRAPA's substantial overall financing requirements.
The proposed Bank loan has been designed to complement the various bilateral
efforts. In addition to the proposed Bank loan for the research programs in
the Northeast, Amazonia and Cerrados, the Brazilians hope to negotiate finan-
cing from IDB for research programs now being prepared for five or six cereal
crops for the Center-south and South.



ANNEX 17
Page 3
B. Research Program Structure
7.        The project would strengthen agricultural research in three main
agro-ecological regions of tropical Brazil: in the semi-arid Northeast, the
humid North (Amazonia) and the intermediate savanna (Campos Cerrados), Central-
West. Priority is to be given to the Northeast, the poorest area of the country,
but work would also be initiated in the Central-West and North regions to esta-
blish the base for an expanded second-phase project. The research would encom-
pass the following program areas:
(a) The development of improved farming systems, including
materials and practices, for the soils and climatic
conditions in the three agro-ecological regions, with
headquarters location for each program, as follows:
Agricultural Research Center for the Semi-Arid Tropics:
at Petrolina, state of Pernambuco, and Juazeiro, state
of Bahia.
Agricultural Research Center for the Humid Tropics:
at Belem, state of Para.
Agricultural Research Center for the Intermediate Savanna
Tropics (Campos Cerrados) Region: at Planaltina, Brasilia,
Federal District.
(b) The development of nationally coordinated commodity research
programs for the improvement of crop and livestock production,
with headquarters location for each program, as follows:
National Research Center for Maize and Sorghum:  at Sete Lagoas,
state of Minas Gerais.
National Research Center for Cotton: at Campina Grande, state
of Paraiba.
National Research Center for Cassava: at Cruz das Almas, state
of Bahia.
National Research Center for Rice and Beans: at Goiania, state
of Goias.
National Research Center for Rubber: at Manaus, state of Ama-
zonas.
National Research Center for Beef Cattle: at Campo Grande,
state of Mato Grosso.



ANNEX 17
Page 4
National Research Center for Dairy Cattle: at Agua Limpa,
state of Minas Gerais.
National Research Center for Sheep and Goats: at Sobral, state
of Ceara.
(c) The strengthening of research at the state level. The 14 research
units at the state level (UEPAEs) included in the project would
conduct adaptive research on improvement of farming systems for
the regions in which they are located.  This would involve colla-
boration with the research programs of the three main agro-ecolo-
gical regions, as appropriate, and participation in the coopera-
tive national commodity research programs to fit available new
technology into the farming potentials of the areas served by the
UEPAE. The UEPAEs would each concentrate attention on a number
of commodities or program areas, as shown in Table 2. Details
as to the staffing of the UEPAEs, are given in Tables 3 and 4.
(d) The development of contract and other collaborative research.
Support would be provided by EMBRAPA for research on problems
of priority concern in agricultural development, as identified
by EMBRAPA, but jointly planned with the unversity or other
institution which would conduct the research under contract or
cooperative agrA eement.
8.        The research station network comprised of EMBRAPA centers and
collaborating institutions would be different for each commodity and
farming system research program and is presented in the respective annex.
The organization chart for EMBRAPA is presented in Chart 1. The president
and three directors furnish executive leadership.
C. Research Program Management
Planning
9.        The leaders of EMBRAPA have given considerable attention to research
program planning and formulation, this being a most critical factor in the
success of EMBRAPA in achieving its objectives, since planning affects not
only what research is done, but when, how, by whom, and how well it is done.
However, the planning of national multi-disciplinary, problem-oriented re-
search programs in the various commodity and problem areas, involving the
integrated efforts of a substantial number of collaborating institutions,
can become a cumbersome, time-consuming process that dissipates excessive
research staff time and other resources, unless the planning procedures are
kept simple and precise.



ANNFX 17
Page  5
10.       National agricultural research programs would support the objectives
and goals of the government with respect to agricultural development, as set
forth in the National Development Plan. The National Committee for Agricul-
tural Research, Technical Assistance and Rural Extension (COMPATER) would
serve as the Technical Advisory Council to EMBRAPA to ensure continuing
awareness of national priority requirements.
11.       The EMBRAPA directorate would furnish general policy and procedural
guidance in the formulation of the total research program. EMBRAPA is
developing a Program Planning and Budgeting System, (PPBS) - with clearly
stated identification of the problem, plan of work, leadership and coop-
erating organizations, and the like -- to facilitate research program plan-
ning, review and budgeting. The PPBS would serve to guide the degree of
involvement desirable for the EMBRAPA headquarters in planning and other
management processes. The station, or headquarters center, director would be
responsible for the overall administrative policy of the center and would
represent EMBRAPA in all aspects of community relations.
12.       The specific research programs for the three agricultural regions
and for the commodities in the project would be designed primarily by the
research scientists concerned with the commodity or problem area. The
Associate Director for Research at the headquarters center would function
as the national research program leader/coordinator and would be given major
responsibility for developing the researcih programs, drawing upoli Llae advice
and guidance of the team of senior research scientists in the various disci-
plines from the participating centers or institutions. Annual workshops for
evaluation of progress and for identification of priority needs and opportuni-
ties for modification of the research would permit a high level of research
scientist participation in planning and redirection of research.
13.       Advisory councils are being established for national commodity and
area research programs to assist in identification of priority problems and
needs, in the general planning of the research programs, and in encouraging
more effective dissemination and application of improved technology. The
councils would serve in an advisory capacity and not in a management role.
The membership of the advisory councils would differ somewhat for the various
commodity and problem area programs, but a typical council would include:
(a) one representative, or more, of producers;
(b) a representative of industry;
(c) a representative of the universities;
(d) a representative of EMBRATER;
(e) the national program leader/coordinator; and
(f) a representative of the EMBRAPA Department of Technology
and Science (DTS) and of other EMBRAPA departments as may
be indicated.



ANNEX 17
Page 6
14.       The advisory councils wqould not only keep the research directed
to the practical priority problems of producers and the industry, but would
provide the nucleus of a constituency to demand research and to assist in
obtaining support for it.
Execution
15.       The review of factors involved in strengthening agricultural re-
search in Brazil, leading to the establishment nf FMPRAPA, identified the
importance of national policies that would guarantee the operation of pro-
grams and projects through decentralized execution, and the maximum use of
existing resources in the different parts of the country. The primary re-
sponsibility for carrying out the national commodity and/or area programs
would be vested in the respective national research center. The partici-
pating or collaborating research centers and institutions would also have
a high degree of autonomy in concluding their part of the national research
program, within the framework of the agreed-upon work plans.
16.       The national research program leader/coordinator would be respon-
sible for maintaining liaison with the participating research scientists
and institutions to insure maximum conformity to agreed-upon national re-
search programs.
Coordination
17.       The national research programs of EMBRAPA will require a high de-
gree of integration and collaboration among (a) the different participating
institutions, including universities and private organizations, and (b)
the scientists from different specialized fields that form the multi-disci-
plinary research teams. Interinstitutional collaboration would be facili-
tated by cooperative agreements that define the role and contribution of the
respective organizations.
18.       The national research program leader/coordinator would have the
primary responsibility for coordination of the research, for ensuring that
the participating scientists carry out their part of the agreed-upon work
plan, and for seeing that the activities are conducted within the terms of
agreements between the collaborating institutions. The Program Planning
and Budgeting System (PPBS) would facilitate the management, including
effective coordination, of multi-disciplinary, multi-institutional
research.
Technical Support and Management
19.       The authorities for program and administrative management functions
at EMBRAPA headquarters are dispersed at the present time, with one EMBRAPA
director responsible for technical programs, another for planning and special
projects, and a third for information and documentation, personnel and train-
ing, data processing, and diffusion of technology. These departments are
identified in Chart 1. As the work of the three regional agricultural pro-
grams, the eight commodity research programs, and the related activities of



ANNEX 17
Page  7
the 14 UEPAEs become more fully operational, it will be desirable to
modify the organization and management system. An organizational struc-
ture, as shown in Chart 2, would serve to facilitate the delegation of
line authority and responsibility for technical and administrative manage-
ment. This has been reviewed with the leaders of EMBRAPA. Chart 3 shows
proposed management structure for research programs.
20.       The director at EMBRAPA headquarters who is in charge of the
Department of Technology and Science (DTS) is the principal officer con-
cerned with technical program management. He will be assisted by a staff
of 12 scientists, specialists in the various disciplines concerned in
agricultural research. This will permit effective technical inputs into
the various research programs and good staff level liaison with the re-
search personnel.
Technical Assistance
21.       The development of EMBRAPA into an effectively functioning
national research corporation for agriculture, with well integrated re-
search teams in the different commodities and farming regions and with
continuing compatible' relationships with the collaborating institutions
involved, is a formidable task. The need to give concurrent attention to
development of 25 research stations, to the training of a multi-disci-
plinary staff alnd suppurting personniel, and to activation of productive
research programs offers a challenge few countries have faced.
22.       The project provides for a research program advisor, a research
scientist-administrator of international stature, to work with the leader-
ship of EMBRAPA in development of policies, procedures, and the organiza-
tion and management structure required for an effective national agricul-
tural research system. This research program advisor would be available
for a period of five years (terms of reference are in Appendix 1).
23.       The development of the agricultural research programs in the
three regions, the formation of their multi-disciplinary teams for farming
systems research, and the establishment of linkages for each of the three
regional centers with the appropriate national commodity research programs
will require substantial organization and management competence. The proj-
ect provides for an internationally experienced agricultural research
scientist with competence in this type of research to be available for a
period of three years for each of the three agricultural research centers.
24.       The development of commodity research programs, nationwide in
scope, conducted by multi-disciplinary teams of scientists from different
collaborating institutions, is new to Brazilian agricultural research.
Effective integration and cooperation of scientists from different disci-
plines and of independent institutions is difficult to achieve and even
more difficult to maintain. The project provides for 10 consultants,
experienced in national commodity research programs, each to be available
for a period of three years to assist in setting up the programs (terms of
reference are in Appendix 2).



ANNEX 17
Page 8
25.       The leaders of EMBRAPA have identified a number of specific fields
or disciplines in which scientific competence and/or experience is presently
limited in Brazil. The project would supply specialists on terms of one
year or more as well as on short-term assignments to meet these needs.
Terms of reference for these specialists are given in Appendix 3. A resume
of the technical assistance to be provided to meet the current need is given
in Table 5.
26.       The external consultant support appears to be well considered
with respect to types of specialists, the terms of assignment, and the
number that could be utilized well during the term of the project. The
types of specialists to be provided could be revised during project imple-
mentation, however, as experience will identify specific needs.
D. Administrative Management and Services
Line Authority and Responsibility
27.       The linkage of the field research centers to the EMBRAPA program
and administrative leaders, as mentioned previously, should be modified as
the EMBRAPA programs grow. The adoption of an organizational structure such
as that presented in Chart 2 would not only facilitate delegation of respon-
sibilities for research program operations, but would also ensure more exped-
itious handling of administration support and services.
Budgets and Financial Management
28.       The manner in which budgets are developed and funds disbursed has
a direct bearing on research program management. The integrated Program
Planning and Budgeting System of EMBRAPA, with financial requirements deter-
mined on the basis of the respective national commodity or area programs,
would permit sound financial management and also facilitate execution of the
research, with maximum authority and responsibility delegated to the national
program leaders and to the individual research scientists. The planning of
budgets and allocation of funds primarily on the basis of individual research
centers would encourage an excessive degree of station autonomy, which would
contradict the close integration of multi-disciplinary, multi-institutional
programs. Most of the work of EMBRAPA within the projectK would be subject
to budgeting on the national commodity program basis, but with some "station"
budgets to provide for the work at the regional agricultural research centers
and the UEPAEs.
29.       Procedures that permit timely and prompt disbursement of funds are
important in ensuring that experiments with seasonal or other time restraints
are not affected adversely because of delays in obtaining supplies, equipment
or other inputs.



ANNEX 17
Page 9
Staffing
30.       General requirements for scientific and technical personnel have
been estimated by EMBRAPA for the various national research programs. These
projections would be subject to modification as experience in implementing
the research identifies the staffing needs more precisely. Similarly, the
most desirable composition of the scientific staff, with respect to re-
searchers trained through the Ph.D., M.Sc., and B.Sc. degree levels, can
be determined best as EMBPRAPA programs are activated.  Most of the re-
search would be production-oriented, with strong emphasis on applied and
adaptive types of research in the field to develop improved technologies.
Such research requires some highly trained scientists in key positions to
supply conceptual and planning leadership, but with substantial junior and
technical support staff to carry the load of field and laboratory research
work. The ratio of about one Ph.D. to two M.Sc. to four B.Sc. degrees
provides an acceptable staff composition for most of the regional area
and commodity research that would be emphasized under the project.
31.       The staffing patterns, as developed under the project for the
respective national commodity and area research programs and for the
UEPAEs, would furnish both the disciplinary team composition and the
distribution of senior, junior and support staff necessary for effective
research. The staffing for the. UEPAEs is designed to furnish the ongoing
research capability necessary for the farming systems studied for the
respective region and much of the adaptive research and field testing
that would be undertaken as the UEPAE station role in coordinated national
research programs. Some additional specialist staff would be necessary
at certain UEPAEs, or at other cooperating institutions, for in-depth
research on more critical limiting factors for a given commodity. Such
specialist scientists would be provided and funded through the appropriate
national research program.
32.       The leaders of EMBRAPA have arranged for consultation with other
research organizations, including the Agricultural Research Service of the
IJ.S. Department of Agriculture, in developing personnel management practices.
Evaluation and promotion procedures based upon "performance of the man on
the job" are being considered. This is an effective means of managing
scientific personnel in a new organization such as EMBRAPA where substantial
numbers of young scientists with advanced degrees but only limited working
experience in research will be employed over a short span of years.
33.       The recruitment procedures for EMBRAPA scientists should be based
upon the same performance and qualification standards as would be used for
evaluation and promotion. The judgment of research program leaders is
important in selecting the scientific staff for a given program or re-
search center, but procedures should be followed to insure that strong
personal biases do not unduly favor or mitigate against potential candidates.



ANNEX 17
Page  10
Training and Staff Development
34.       The training and staff development program supported under the
project is an ambitious one, but the availability of trained scientists is
a major limiting factor in the implementation of the national research
responsibilities of EMBRAPA. The number of Ph.D. and M.Sc. degree per-
sonnel to be trained provides for the staff required for the research
programs and stations under the project (448) plus an additional number
(338) for other programs of EMBRAPA in the project area. In addition to
the advanced degree training, there will be need for in-service types
of experience and training for technical and other support staff, most
of which could be conducted at research centers in Brazil. For details
of the fellowship program, see Tables 6 and 7.
E. Diffusion and Application of Technology
EMBRATER Responsibilities
35.       In order to improve the rural extension system, the Ministry of
Agriculture has established the Brazilian Technical Assistance and Rural
Extension Corporation (EIIBRATER). This organization is still in the
formative stage, but it would work in close collaboration with EMBRAPA
in carrying out activities concerned with farm sector development, in-
cluding the diffusion of improved technology.
EMBRAPA Responsibilities
36.       EMBRAPA has a Department of Diffusion of Technology that provides
the linkage between the various national research programs and EMBRATER and
other organizations concerned with rural development. The National Committee
of Agricultural Research, Technical Assistance and Rural Extension (COMPATER),
would serve as the formal agency to coordinate the functions of EMBRAPA,
EMBRATER, and other organizations with mutual interest in development and
diffusion of improved technology.
37.       The agricultural research centers for the three regions, the
national commodity research program headquarters stations, and the state
research units or UEPAEs under the project, each has staff members who would
be concerned with diffusion of technology. These persons would work with
the research staff in carrying out verification trials for new materials
and practices and with the extension personnel in planning and conducting
field demonstrations with cooperating farmers for promotion and dissemina-
tion of improved technology. They also would assist in the preparation of
appropriate extension bulletins. In addition, the training officers, and/
or extension specialists at the research stations would be directly involved
in the technology diffusion activities.



ANNEX 17
Page 11
The UEPAES
38.       The role of the UEPAEs would be especially significant in linking
the various commodity research programs and extension organizations. The
UEPAEs, functioning at the state level, would provide the outreach for adap-
tive research for relevant commodities, serving as participants in the various
national integrated research programs. They also would conduct research on
farming systems, putting the improved materials and methods together into
packages of practices best suited for improving farming in the region. The
staff of the UEPAEs, including the research workers, would assist in train-
ing the extension personnel concerned with diffusion of technology (see Tables
3 and 4).
F. Linkages with International Programs and Scientists
International Research Institutes
39.       International agricultural research institutes or centers have been
established for many of the commodities under the project. EMBRAPA leaders
are in contact with specialists of the relevant international centers, and
the project provides, through its technical assistance component, support for
scientists from these centers who serve as consultants in the various special-
ized disciplines or in reviewing national integrated research programs. A
list of the international centers most closely concerned with work in agro-
ecological areas and on commodities of interest to the Brazil project is given
in Table 8.
Other National Agricultural Research Systems
40.       In the past decade, a number of countries in Latin America, Asia
and Africa have taken steps to strengthen their national agricultural re-
search capabilities and organizations. The continuous contact of EMBRAPA
program leaders with technical and administrative leaders of these emerging
national programs and systems will be of mutual benefit in fitting organiza-
tion and management practices to evolving, staff and facility capabilities
suited to conditions of developing nations.
Selected External Scientists
41.       The project provides for a wide range of scientific consultants for
short-term as well as long-term assignments in special fields identified by
EMBRAPA leaders as requiring such external assistance. The opportunity to
draw upon worldwide scientific resources for consultation and for formation
of continuing scientific communications linkages should ensure a strong base
of experienced guidance in formulating the various national research programs
of EMBRAPA (terms of reference for the scientific consultants are in Appendix 3).



ANNEX 17
Page  12
G. Monitoring and Evaluation
42.       The administration of EMBRAPA would ensure that appropriate
monitoring and evaluation functions are carried out as indicated below.
All of the five main administrative departments of EMBRAPA, plus the
Technical Support Unit (TSU), would be involved in supplying data under
the criteria indicated; it would be essential that the Department of
Technology and Science (DTS), with the assistance of the Research Pro-
grams Advisor, establish an evaluation unit to be assigned the task of
coordinating the inputs from the TSU and the other departments concerned,
such as (a) Department of Planning and Methods, (b) Department of Informa-
tion and Documentation, (c) Department of Technology Diffusion, (d) Depart-
ment of Data Processing, and (e) Department of Human Resources. Key
indicators, specifying projected goals, would be provided to the appro-
priate department for periodic reporting of results as indicated.
Monitoring
43.       In order to ensure that project implementation meets projected
goals as closely as possible, data on the following key indicators would
be registered, and reported on a quarterly basis to Bank under normal
procedure:
(a) The degree to which professional and administrative
staff levels meet project goals and adequate
space and supply facilities are made available to
comply with level of staffing at each facility.
(b) Review of fellowship and in-service-training programs
to indicate not only numbers of staff participating
but also appropriateness and quality of educational
programs being provided.
(c) Timely programming of technical services such as
program consultants, both long-term and short-term.
(d) Progress of civil works construction at the respective
experiment station sites in accordance with projected
implementation timetables, including early acquisition
of land holdings where necessary.
(e) Equipping of laboratories and field facilities at these
sites to ensure they become operational within specified
projected time limits.
(f) Progress on Research Farm Development.



ANNEX 17
Page 13
(g) Acquisition of necessary farm equipment vehicles
and supplies.
(h) Degree to which library documentation and infor-
mation services are available at the various sites,
consistent with staffing level.
(i) Finally, there should be a direct feedback from the
technical program evaluation unit (under DTS) to
report the extent of progress in the execution of
the approved research program.
Research Program Evaluation
44.       Whereas monitoring is provided to ensure the necessary oversight
for expenditures and physical progress of project implementation, periodic
evaluation of research programs is designed to control the performance of
these projects and to provide the necessary information on which future
program emphasis may be determined, during the planning stage. Of equal
importance to the evaluation process is the choice of criteria used in this
evaluation. In addition, the selected criteria may be weighted to reflect
national and regional priorities and the contribution of the research
program to these development plans-  Unlike the case of monitoring, key
indicators cannot easily be predetermined but rather should be chosen for
each program as they develop. Basic areas for choice of criteria, however,
in the planning state, come from answering questions concerning the follow-
ing broad aspects: technical feasibility, research direction and balance,
timing and impact on yields. During research program execution these
criteria would be modified, reoriented and applied as appropriate in order
to evaluate: significant progress toward program or project goals; degree
of utilization given to national and international sources of relevant data
and research methods; interpretation of experimental data; presentation of
meaningful progress reports; testing and field demonstration of research
results; degree of success achieved in the dissemination and adoption of
new technology by producers; and finally the impact on yields and production.
Program evaluation should be dynamic in addressing the needs of individual
programs and should be so designed as to provide management with information
on the relative value of the research being undertaken and indicate when
programs may be strengthened, and/or reoriented as necessary. Information
obtained would also provide the basis for cost/benefit analysis as desired.
45.       Annual workshops for review of progress, and for redirection of
resources to high priority problem areas, provide for a continuing process
of evaluation and monitoring of research programs. The principal members
of the research team, including representation from the collaborating in-
stitutions, EMBRAPA headquarters representatives, members of the respective
advisory councils, and external scientists as may be indicated, would
participate in the workshops. The national research program/leader coordi-
nator would be responsible for organizing the workshop. In addition to the



ANNEX 17
Page 14
regular workshop type of review, it would be desirable to conduct selected
in-depth reviews, of a total national commodity program, or of the work on
a particularly stubborn disease, pest control, soil management or other
problem. The short-term consultants provided for in the project would be
useful in program evaluation, especially if they have sufficient time in
the field to observe the research under way and follow this with participa-
tion in the program review and planning workshop.
46.       An appropriate, external review of the technical research
programs would be undertaken by a review team, comprised of externally
recruited consultant scientists, during the third to fifth year of
project implementation.
January 15, 1976

BRAZIL
AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH I PROJECT
Terms of Reference for Research Programs Advisor
1.        The Brazilian Agricultural Research Corporation (EMBRAPA) would re-
quire the services of a research programs advisor for a period of five years
to assist the President of EMBRAPA and his staff in the organization and
management of the research and related programs.
2.        The research programs advisor would be an internationally experienced
agricultural research scientist with proven administrative competence. He
would assist EMBRAPA in strengthening its research programs planning and its
operational and administrative competence. He should have the ability to com-
municate effectively with others, to identify research needs and potentials,
and to organize and assess progress of research programs.
3.        The research programs advisor would assist the leadership of EMBRAPA
in such areas as:
(a) determining the priority needs for research and
designing effective multi-disciplinary, problem-
oriented research programs;
(b) allocating funds, including external support, to
ensure adequate levels of research performance;
(c) planning and improving research station laboratories
and field facilities for multi-disciplinary research
teams;
(d) formulating personnel policies and procedures for
recruitment, appointment and pronotion that will
furnish the professional environment conducive to
productive research;
(e) evaluating progress of research and redirecting
efforts to meet changing priority requirements; and
(f) selecting candidates for fellowship awards and
furnishing guidance in planning individual and
group training programs.



ANNEX 17
Appendix 1
Page 2
4.        The research programs advisor would also directly assist the
leadership of EMBRAPA by advising, as necessary, on such matters as:
(a) achieving effective coordination of the commodity and
other research programs conducted by multi-disciplinary
research teams in national or regional programs involving
collaborating research stations of EMBRAPA, the universities,
the UEPAEs, and other institutions and agencies;
(b) establishing cooperative linkages with the relevant inter-
national agricultural research centers and institutes and
other international and national agricultural research
and educational institutions in the improvement of the
research and development programs of EMBRAPA; and
(c) developing and maintaining close collaboration with the
organizations responsible for making the results and
products of research available to farmers, including
cooperation also with agencies that furnish credit and
other inputs and services to farmers. Special attention
should be given to the provision of improved materials,
methods and inputs to small farmers.
5.        He would assist EMBRAPA in the withdrawal, utilization and monitor-
ing of the proceeds of the Bank loan for construction works, equipment and
technical services and in maintaining mutual understanding of the cooperative
relationship and program objectives among the technical and administrative
officers of EMBRAPA and Bank officials.
December 15, 1975

Appendix 2
Page 1
BRAZIL
AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH I PROJECT
Terms of Reference for Consultants for Agricultural Research
1.        The Brazilian Agricultural Research Corporation (EMBRAPA) would re-
quire substantial scientific and management capability during the early years
of the project when it would be developing the facilities, staff resources,
and core research activities of three agricultural research centers and eight
national commodity research programs. Since many of the more experienced
Brazilian scientists would be out of the country pursuing advanced studies,
internationally experienced agricultural research scientists, with competence
in the organization and operation of problem-oriented, multi-disciplinary re-
search programs of national scope should therefore be recruited to assist
the directors of the research centers and the national commodity programs.
2.        The agricultural research program consultants would be recruited
directly or through international or bilateral assistance, under terms and
conditions acceptable to the Bank, to assist in:
(a) identifying the priority problem areas for research
and planning the multi-disciplinary team competence
for the field and laboratory research programs;
(b) determining requirements and setting up priority
schedules, as well as selection procedures for
staff development;
(c) planning field and laboratory facilities, including
equipment, and the schedule for station development;
(d) establishing policies and procedures to achieve
maximum integration of the efforts of scientists
in the multi-disciplinary research teams;
(e) formulating agreements and procedures to achieve
maximum collaboration between the main research
center, sub-centers, UEPAEs, universities and other
research and educational institutions mutually con-
cerned with the national research program;



ANNEX 17
Appendix 2
Page 2
(f) developing cooperative linkages with relevant inter-
national agricultural research centers and institutes
and with other external international and national
agricultural research and educational institutions; and
(g) achieving effective collaboration with the organizations
responsible for making available to farmers the results
and products of research through mutual planning and
execution of training programs, field trials, and
demonstrations, with special attention to the needs of
small farmers for improved technology, credit, and other
inputs.
3.        Three research program consultants would be employed, one each
for the three agricultural research centers, for a minimum period of three
years. An additional five consultants would be employed, each for a minimum
period of two years, to assist the nine commodity research programs. Assign-
ments would be mutually agreed upon by the leaders of EMBRAPA and the Bank.
December 15, 1975



ANNEX 17
Appendix 3
BRAZIL
AGRICULTURAL RESEARCH I PROJECT
Terms of Reference for Scientific Consultants
1.         The Brazilian Agricultural Research Corporation (EMBRAPA) would re-
quire guidance and assistance in establishing effective research in the many
component disciplines related to agriculture that must be integrated in the
respective area development and commodity improvement programs. The need
for such assistance from experienced scientists is fully recognized by the
leaders of EMBRAPA and provision is made for them on both short-term and
long-term assignments in the project.
2.         The scientific consultants would be recruited directly, or through
international or bilateral assistance, for priority problem areas or for
integrated multi-disciplinary research programs, on schedules to be deter-
mined by the leaders of EMBRAPA. They would assist in:
(a) determining the specific factors within the respective
disciplines to receive priority research attention and
helping to design appropriate experiments;
(b) identifying basic breeding stocks and other materials as
well as improved methodologies from international sources
needed for pursuing research;
(c) establishing personal contacts and linkages with research
specialists working on similar problems elsewhere in the
world;
(d) conducting critical reviews and evaluations of the research
in specific disciplines and/or programs to guide redirection
of resources to more critical, feasible research efforts;
(e) developing workshops and training programs for accelerating
the training and development of research personnel, including
middle-level technical and support staff; and
(f) planning extended field trials and demonstrations in
cooperation with the organizations responsible for ensuring
effective use of improved technology and other production
inputs at the farm level.
December 15, 1975
